## **Packet L04‚ÄëS4 ‚Äî Degenerate projector**

```latex
\section*{L04-S4 Degenerate projector ‚Äî Problem}
Let $\hat A$ have eigenvalue $a$ with orthonormal eigenstates $\{|a,1\rangle,|a,2\rangle\}$.
Construct the projector $P_a$ and show it is Hermitian and idempotent.

\newpage
\section*{Suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Sum dyads $|a,\alpha\rangle\langle a,\alpha|$.
\item Use orthonormality.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Advanced suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Check $P_a^2$ term by term.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Detailed solution}
\[
P_a = |a,1\rangle\langle a,1| + |a,2\rangle\langle a,2|.
\]
Hermiticity is immediate. For idempotence:
\[
P_a^2 = \sum_{\alpha,\beta}|a,\alpha\rangle\langle a,\alpha|a,\beta\rangle\langle a,\beta|
= \sum_{\alpha}|a,\alpha\rangle\langle a,\alpha| = P_a.
\]
```

***

## **Packet L04‚ÄëS8 ‚Äî L√ºders rule (degenerate)**

```latex
\section*{L04-S8 L√ºders rule ‚Äî Problem}
Let $P_a$ be the projector onto a degenerate eigenspace of $\hat A$.
Show that the post‚Äëmeasurement state
\[
|\psi'\rangle=\frac{P_a|\psi\rangle}{\sqrt{\langle\psi|P_a|\psi\rangle}}
\]
is normalized.

\newpage
\section*{Suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Compute $\langle\psi'|\psi'\rangle$.
\item Use $P_a^2=P_a$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Advanced suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Insert $P_a^\dagger=P_a$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Detailed solution}
\[
\langle\psi'|\psi'\rangle
=\frac{\langle\psi|P_a P_a|\psi\rangle}{\langle\psi|P_a|\psi\rangle}
=\frac{\langle\psi|P_a|\psi\rangle}{\langle\psi|P_a|\psi\rangle}=1.
\]
```

***

## **Packet L04‚ÄëC4 ‚Äî L√ºders vs naive collapse**

```latex
\section*{L04-C4 L√ºders vs naive ‚Äî Problem}
Compare L√ºders rule with a naive ``collapse to one eigenvector'' rule for a degenerate measurement.
Explain why the naive rule is physically incorrect.

\newpage
\section*{Suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Ask: what information does the measurement provide?
\item Consider repeatability.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Advanced suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Show naive collapse introduces extra information not measured.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Detailed solution}
A degenerate measurement determines only the eigenvalue $a$, not the label $\alpha$.
Collapsing to a specific $|a,\alpha\rangle$ would add information not present in the measurement outcome.
L√ºders rule projects onto the full eigenspace, preserving exactly the information gained and no more.
```

# **Lecture 5 ‚Äî Completeness, Change of Basis, and Unification of Representations**

### Dirac (abstract) ‚Üî Matrix mechanics ‚Üî Wavefunction (continuous basis)

***

## 90‚Äëminute pacing

2.  Translate: abstract ket ‚Üî coefficient vector ‚Üî wavefunction
3.  Perform unitary basis changes and compute transformed components
4.  Translate operators: abstract operator ‚Üî matrix elements ‚Üî integral kernel
5.  Compute inner products and expectation values in all three representations

# C) Lecture notes (Narrative + derivations) ‚Äî LaTeX sources

## C1) Single-source chapter with instructor toggle

Copy as: `L05_chapter.tex`

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}
\usepackage{geometry}
\geometry{margin=1in}
\usepackage{amsmath,amssymb,physics,hyperref}
\usepackage{enumitem}
\usepackage{tcolorbox}
\usepackage{booktabs}

\newif\ifinstructor

\newtcolorbox{pacingbox}{colback=blue!3!white,colframe=blue!60!black,title=90-minute pacing}
\newtcolorbox{outcomesbox}{colback=green!3!white,colframe=green!50!black,title=Core outcomes}
\newtcolorbox{warnbox}{colback=red!2!white,colframe=red!60!black,title=Common pitfalls}
\newtcolorbox{mapbox}{colback=purple!2!white,colframe=purple!60!black,title=Unified dictionary: Dirac $\leftrightarrow$ Matrix $\leftrightarrow$ Wavefunction}

\title{Lecture 5: Completeness, Change of Basis, and Unification of Representations}
\author{}
\date{}

\begin{document}
\maketitle

\begin{pacingbox}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
\item 0--15: What is a representation? State vs coordinates
\item 15--35: Discrete completeness; insert identity
\item 35--55: Unitary change of basis; matrices and similarity
\item 55--75: Continuous completeness; wavefunction as projection
\item 75--90: Operator kernels; expectation values in $x$-rep; synthesis
\end{itemize}
\end{pacingbox}

\begin{outcomesbox}
\begin{enumerate}[leftmargin=*]
\item Expand states using $\sum_n|n\rangle\langle n|=\mathbb I$ and $\int dx\,|x\rangle\langle x|=\mathbb I$.
\item Translate between $|\psi\rangle$, coefficient vectors $\{c_n\}$, and wavefunctions $\psi(x)=\langle x|\psi\rangle$.
\item Translate operators: $A_{mn}=\langle m|\hat A|n\rangle$ and kernel $A(x,x')=\langle x|\hat A|x'\rangle$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{outcomesbox}

\section{Motivation: same state, different representations}
A quantum state is the abstract object $|\psi\rangle$. A \emph{representation} is obtained by choosing a basis and
computing components. Different bases correspond to different measurement contexts.

\begin{warnbox}
Do not confuse the state with its coordinate list. The list changes when you change basis, even though the state
does not.
\end{warnbox}

\section{Discrete basis: completeness and inserting identity}
Let $\{|n\rangle\}$ be an orthonormal basis:
\[
\langle m|n\rangle=\delta_{mn},\qquad \sum_n |n\rangle\langle n|=\mathbb I.
\]
Insert the identity to expand any state:
\[
|\psi\rangle = \mathbb I|\psi\rangle = \sum_n |n\rangle\langle n|\psi\rangle.
\]
Define components (amplitudes in this basis):
\[
c_n=\langle n|\psi\rangle,\qquad |\psi\rangle=\sum_n c_n|n\rangle.
\]

\subsection{Inner product in components}
Insert identity twice:
\[
\langle\phi|\psi\rangle
=\sum_n \langle\phi|n\rangle\langle n|\psi\rangle
=\sum_n \phi_n^*\,\psi_n.
\]
This is the coordinate formula for inner products.

\section{Change of basis: unitary transformations}
Let $\{|n\rangle\}$ and $\{|\alpha\rangle\}$ be orthonormal bases. Define the overlap matrix
\[
U_{\alpha n}=\langle \alpha|n\rangle.
\]
Then
\[
\psi_\alpha=\langle \alpha|\psi\rangle
=\sum_n \langle \alpha|n\rangle \langle n|\psi\rangle
=\sum_n U_{\alpha n}\,c_n.
\]
So, in vector form:
\[
\mathbf c^{(\alpha)} = U\,\mathbf c^{(n)}.
\]
Because both bases are orthonormal, $U$ is unitary.

\section{Operators: abstract $\leftrightarrow$ matrix}
Define matrix elements in basis $\{|n\rangle\}$:
\[
A_{mn}=\langle m|\hat A|n\rangle.
\]
Then for coefficient vectors $\mathbf c$,
\[
(\hat A|\psi\rangle)_m = \sum_n A_{mn}c_n,
\]
i.e. $\mathbf c' = A\mathbf c$.

\subsection{Similarity under basis change}
If $U$ changes basis, the matrix of the same abstract operator becomes
\[
A' = UAU^\dagger
\quad\text{(convention: coefficients transform as } \mathbf c'=U\mathbf c\text{)}.
\]

\section{Continuous basis: wavefunctions as projections}
Introduce position kets $|x\rangle$ (formal for now) satisfying completeness:
\[
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty} dx\,|x\rangle\langle x|=\mathbb I,
\qquad \psi(x)=\langle x|\psi\rangle.
\]
Then expansion becomes
\[
|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,|x\rangle\psi(x).
\]

\subsection{Inner product in wavefunctions}
Insert the continuous identity:
\[
\langle\phi|\psi\rangle
=\int dx\,\langle\phi|x\rangle\langle x|\psi\rangle
=\int dx\,\phi^*(x)\psi(x).
\]

\section{Operators in the $x$-representation: kernels}
Define the kernel
\[
A(x,x')=\langle x|\hat A|x'\rangle.
\]
Then
\[
(\hat A\psi)(x)=\langle x|\hat A|\psi\rangle
=\int dx'\,\langle x|\hat A|x'\rangle\langle x'|\psi\rangle
=\int dx'\,A(x,x')\psi(x').
\]
Expectation values become
\[
\langle \hat A\rangle
=\langle\psi|\hat A|\psi\rangle
=\int dx\,dx'\,\psi^*(x)\,A(x,x')\,\psi(x').
\]

\begin{mapbox}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Abstract (Dirac)} & \textbf{Matrix basis }|n\rangle & \textbf{Wavefunction basis }|x\rangle\\ \midrule
$|\psi\rangle$ & $c_n=\langle n|\psi\rangle$ & $\psi(x)=\langle x|\psi\rangle$\\
$\mathbb I$ & $\sum_n|n\rangle\langle n|$ & $\int dx\,|x\rangle\langle x|$\\
$\hat A$ & $A_{mn}=\langle m|\hat A|n\rangle$ & $A(x,x')=\langle x|\hat A|x'\rangle$\\
$\hat A|\psi\rangle$ & $c'_m=\sum_n A_{mn}c_n$ & $(A\psi)(x)=\int dx'\,A(x,x')\psi(x')$\\
$\langle\phi|\psi\rangle$ & $\sum_n \phi_n^*\psi_n$ & $\int dx\,\phi^*(x)\psi(x)$\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{mapbox}

\ifinstructor
\appendix
\section{Instructor-only notes}
Stress: (i) the state is the same object; (ii) representation is the choice of basis; (iii) the identity resolution
is the engine that translates expressions between representations. Preview Lecture 6: momentum basis and Fourier transform.
\fi

\end{document}
```

## D1) Beamer deck (LaTeX)

Copy as `L05_slides_beamer.tex`:

```latex
\documentclass{beamer}
\usetheme{Madrid}
\usepackage{amsmath}
\title{Lecture 5: Completeness and Unified Representations}
\begin{document}

\begin{frame}\titlepage\end{frame}

\begin{frame}{Big idea}
One state $|\psi\rangle$; many representations:
\[
c_n=\langle n|\psi\rangle,\qquad \psi(x)=\langle x|\psi\rangle
\]
\end{frame}

\begin{frame}{Completeness (discrete and continuous)}
\[
\sum_n|n\rangle\langle n|=\mathbb I,
\qquad
\int dx\,|x\rangle\langle x|=\mathbb I
\]
\end{frame}

\begin{frame}{Basis change}
\[
U_{\alpha n}=\langle \alpha|n\rangle,\quad
\psi_\alpha = \sum_n U_{\alpha n}c_n
\]
\end{frame}

\begin{frame}{Operators}
Matrix elements:
\[
A_{mn}=\langle m|\hat A|n\rangle
\Rightarrow c' = A c
\]
Kernel:
\[
A(x,x')=\langle x|\hat A|x'\rangle
\Rightarrow (A\psi)(x)=\int dx'\,A(x,x')\psi(x')
\]
\end{frame}

\begin{frame}{Expectation value in $x$-rep}
\[
\langle A\rangle=\int dx\,dx'\,\psi^*(x)A(x,x')\psi(x')
\]
\end{frame}

\end{document}
```

## D2) PowerPoint outline

Copy as `L05_slides_ppt_outline.md`:

```md
# Lecture 5: Completeness & Unified Representations

## Slide 1 ‚Äî Title
- One abstract state |œà‚ü©; many representations

## Slide 2 ‚Äî Discrete representation
- cn = ‚ü®n|œà‚ü©
- |œà‚ü© = Œ£n |n‚ü©cn
- Œ£n |n‚ü©‚ü®n| = I

## Slide 3 ‚Äî Continuous (wavefunction) representation
- œà(x) = ‚ü®x|œà‚ü©
- |œà‚ü© = ‚à´ dx |x‚ü©œà(x)
- ‚à´ dx |x‚ü©‚ü®x| = I

## Slide 4 ‚Äî Inner products
- ‚ü®œÜ|œà‚ü© = Œ£n œÜn* œàn
- ‚ü®œÜ|œà‚ü© = ‚à´ dx œÜ*(x) œà(x)

## Slide 5 ‚Äî Basis change
- UŒ±n = ‚ü®Œ±|n‚ü©
- œàŒ± = Œ£n UŒ±n cn
- Unitary preserves norms

## Slide 6 ‚Äî Operators in matrices
- Amn = ‚ü®m|A|n‚ü©

- A(x,x') = ‚ü®x|A|x'‚ü©
```

# E) Concept Questions (CQ) ‚Äî 10

1.  What is the difference between a state and its representation?
2.  What does it mean to ‚Äúinsert the identity‚Äù in bra‚Äìket notation?
3.  Why does $$\sum_n|n\rangle\langle n|$$ equal $$\mathbb I$$?
4.  How do coefficients transform under a change of basis?
5.  Why is the basis-change matrix unitary?
6.  How do operator matrices transform under basis change?
7.  What is $$\psi(x)=\langle x|\psi\rangle$$ conceptually?
8.  What does the operator kernel $$A(x,x')$$ represent?
9.  How do you compute $$\langle\phi|\psi\rangle$$ in discrete vs continuous representations?
10. What are the dangers of treating $$|x\rangle$$ as a normal vector (preview)?

***

# F) **Simple Problem Set (SPS) ‚Äî 10**

S1 Expand a state using discrete completeness; compute components  
S2 Compute inner product using identity insertion (discrete)  
S3 Change of basis: compute new coefficients using $$U_{\alpha n}=\langle\alpha|n\rangle$$  
S4 Show unitarity preserves normalization in a basis change  
S5 Derive matrix multiplication rule using inserted identity  
S6 Translate operator expectation value: $$\langle\psi|A|\psi\rangle\leftrightarrow c^\dagger A c$$  
S7 Define wavefunction $$\psi(x)=\langle x|\psi\rangle$$ and expand ket $$|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,|x\rangle\psi(x)$$  
S8 Derive $$\langle\phi|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,\phi^*(x)\psi(x)$$ using continuous identity  
S9 Derive action of operator in $$x$$-rep: $$(A\psi)(x)=\int dx'\,A(x,x')\psi(x')$$  
S10 Evaluate expectation value in $$x$$-rep: $$\langle A\rangle=\int dx\,dx'\,\psi^*(x)A(x,x')\psi(x')$$

***

# G) **Complex Problem Set (CPS) ‚Äî 5**

C1 Prove basis change preserves inner products (unitary invariance)  
C2 Prove operator similarity transform under basis change: $$A' = UAU^\dagger$$ (with fixed convention)  
C3 Prove Parseval identity in discrete and continuous forms (sum/integral)  
C4 Show that the transformation kernel $$K(x,n)=\langle x|n\rangle$$ acts like a unitary map: $$\int dx\,K^*(x,m)K(x,n)=\delta_{mn}$$  
C5 (MSc/PhD) Discuss rigor: why $$|x\rangle$$ is generalized and what ‚Äúkernel‚Äù means (structured essay)

# H) Projects

## Simple Project (SPJ): ‚ÄúRepresentation Translator‚Äù

Build a small notebook/script that:

*   takes a random normalized vector $$c\in\mathbb C^N$$
*   applies a random unitary $$U$$ to produce $$c'=Uc$$
*   verifies normalization and invariance of inner products
*   includes a ‚Äúwavefunction-like‚Äù transform using an arbitrary orthonormal transform matrix $$K$$ (discrete analog of $$\langle x|n\rangle$$)

Deliverables: code + plots + brief report.

## Complex Project (CPJ): ‚ÄúOperator in three representations‚Äù

Choose a finite-dimensional operator $$A$$ (Hermitian):

1.  Abstract description: $$\hat A$$
2.  Matrix in basis $$|n\rangle$$: $$A_{mn}$$
3.  Kernel in a ‚Äúcoordinate basis‚Äù $$|x_j\rangle$$: $$A(x_i,x_j)$$ (discrete coordinate grid)

Explain how:

*   vectors transform,
*   operator transforms as similarity,
*   expectation value stays invariant.

Deliverables: 8‚Äì12 page report + appendix computations.

## **S1 ‚Äî Discrete expansion via completeness**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb,physics}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L05-S1 Discrete expansion ‚Äî Problem}
Let $\{|n\rangle\}$ be an ONB with $\sum_n|n\rangle\langle n|=I$. Show $|\psi\rangle=\sum_n |n\rangle\langle n|\psi\rangle$ and identify $c_n$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Insert $I$ in front of $|\psi\rangle$.
\item Define $c_n=\langle n|\psi\rangle$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Interpret $c_n$ as amplitude for outcome $n$ in that measurement basis.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
$|\psi\rangle=I|\psi\rangle=\left(\sum_n|n\rangle\langle n|\right)|\psi\rangle=\sum_n|n\rangle\langle n|\psi\rangle$.
Define $c_n=\langle n|\psi\rangle$, giving $|\psi\rangle=\sum_n c_n|n\rangle$.
\end{document}
```

## **S2 ‚Äî Inner product in components**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb,physics}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L05-S2 Inner product (discrete) ‚Äî Problem}
Let $|\psi\rangle=\sum_n\psi_n|n\rangle$ and $|\phi\rangle=\sum_n\phi_n|n\rangle$. Prove $\langle\phi|\psi\rangle=\sum_n \phi_n^*\psi_n$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Write $\langle\phi|=\sum_n \phi_n^*\langle n|$.
\item Multiply out and use $\langle n|m\rangle=\delta_{nm}$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Alternatively insert identity: $\langle\phi|\psi\rangle=\sum_n\langle\phi|n\rangle\langle n|\psi\rangle$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
$\langle\phi|=\sum_n\phi_n^*\langle n|$. Then
$\langle\phi|\psi\rangle=\sum_{n,m}\phi_n^*\psi_m\langle n|m\rangle=\sum_n\phi_n^*\psi_n$.
\end{document}
```

## **S3 ‚Äî Change of basis coefficients**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L05-S3 Basis change coefficients ‚Äî Problem}
Let $\{|n\rangle\}$ and $\{|\alpha\rangle\}$ be ONBs. Define $U_{\alpha n}=\langle\alpha|n\rangle$ and $c_n=\langle n|\psi\rangle$.
Show $\psi_\alpha=\langle\alpha|\psi\rangle=\sum_n U_{\alpha n}c_n$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Insert $I=\sum_n|n\rangle\langle n|$ between $\langle\alpha|$ and $|\psi\rangle$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Interpret $U$ as change-of-basis matrix between measurement contexts.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
$\psi_\alpha=\langle\alpha|\psi\rangle=\sum_n\langle\alpha|n\rangle\langle n|\psi\rangle=\sum_n U_{\alpha n}c_n$.
\end{document}
```

## **S4 ‚Äî Unitary preserves normalization**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L05-S4 Unitary preserves norm ‚Äî Problem}
Let $c' = Uc$ with $U^\dagger U=I$. Show $\sum_\alpha |c'_\alpha|^2=\sum_n |c_n|^2$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Use vector notation: $\|c\|^2=c^\dagger c$.
\item Compute $(Uc)^\dagger(Uc)$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Interpret as basis-independence of $\langle\psi|\psi\rangle$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
$\|c'\|^2=(Uc)^\dagger(Uc)=c^\dagger U^\dagger U c=c^\dagger c=\|c\|^2$.
\end{document}
```

## **S5 ‚Äî Matrix multiplication from completeness**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb,physics}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L05-S5 Matrix product rule ‚Äî Problem}
Let $A_{mn}=\langle m|\hat A|n\rangle$ and $B_{mn}=\langle m|\hat B|n\rangle$ in ONB $\{|n\rangle\}$.
Show $(AB)_{mn}=\sum_k A_{mk}B_{kn}$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Write $(AB)_{mn}=\langle m|\hat A\hat B|n\rangle$.
\item Insert $I=\sum_k |k\rangle\langle k|$ between $\hat A$ and $\hat B$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Recognize the derivation of standard matrix multiplication from Dirac notation.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
$(AB)_{mn}=\langle m|\hat A\hat B|n\rangle=\sum_k \langle m|\hat A|k\rangle\langle k|\hat B|n\rangle=\sum_k A_{mk}B_{kn}$.
\end{document}
```

## **S6 ‚Äî Expectation value: Dirac ‚Üî matrix**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L05-S6 Expectation value equivalence ‚Äî Problem}
Let $|\psi\rangle=\sum_n c_n|n\rangle$ and $A_{mn}=\langle m|\hat A|n\rangle$. Show
$\langle\psi|\hat A|\psi\rangle=\sum_{mn} c_m^*A_{mn}c_n = c^\dagger A c$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Expand bras/kets and use bilinearity.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Insert identities on both sides of $\hat A$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
$\langle\psi|=\sum_m c_m^*\langle m|$, so
$\langle\psi|\hat A|\psi\rangle=\sum_{mn} c_m^*\langle m|\hat A|n\rangle c_n=\sum_{mn}c_m^*A_{mn}c_n=c^\dagger A c$.
\end{document}
```

## **S7 ‚Äî Wavefunction as projection**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb,physics}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L05-S7 Wavefunction definition ‚Äî Problem}
Assume $\int dx\,|x\rangle\langle x|=I$. Define $\psi(x)=\langle x|\psi\rangle$ and show
$|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,|x\rangle\psi(x)$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Insert the identity in front of $|\psi\rangle$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Interpret $\psi(x)$ as the coordinate of $|\psi\rangle$ in the position basis.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
$|\psi\rangle=I|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,|x\rangle\langle x|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,|x\rangle\psi(x)$.
\end{document}
```

## **S8 ‚Äî Inner product as integral**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb,physics}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L05-S8 Inner product (continuous) ‚Äî Problem}
Assume $\int dx\,|x\rangle\langle x|=I$. Show $\langle\phi|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,\phi^*(x)\psi(x)$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Insert the identity between $\langle\phi|$ and $|\psi\rangle$.
\item Use $\langle\phi|x\rangle=\phi^*(x)$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Note the analogy to the discrete sum formula.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
$\langle\phi|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,\langle\phi|x\rangle\langle x|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,\phi^*(x)\psi(x)$.
\end{document}
```

## **S9 ‚Äî Operator action as kernel integral**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb,physics}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L05-S9 Operator kernel action ‚Äî Problem}
Define $A(x,x')=\langle x|\hat A|x'\rangle$. Show $(A\psi)(x)=\int dx'\,A(x,x')\psi(x')$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Write $(A\psi)(x)=\langle x|\hat A|\psi\rangle$.
\item Insert $I=\int dx'|x'\rangle\langle x'|$ after $\hat A$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Emphasize the analogy with $c'=Ac$ in discrete bases.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
$(A\psi)(x)=\langle x|\hat A|\psi\rangle=\int dx'\,\langle x|\hat A|x'\rangle\langle x'|\psi\rangle=\int dx'\,A(x,x')\psi(x')$.
\end{document}
```

## **S10 ‚Äî Expectation value as double integral**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb,physics}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L05-S10 Expectation value (kernel) ‚Äî Problem}
Show $\langle\psi|\hat A|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,dx'\,\psi^*(x)A(x,x')\psi(x')$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Insert $I=\int dx\,|x\rangle\langle x|$ on both sides of $\hat A$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Compare to $c^\dagger A c$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
$\langle\psi|\hat A|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,dx'\,\langle\psi|x\rangle\langle x|\hat A|x'\rangle\langle x'|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,dx'\,\psi^*(x)A(x,x')\psi(x')$.
\end{document}
```

***

## **C1 ‚Äî Unitary invariance of inner products**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L05-C1 Inner product invariance ‚Äî Problem}
Let $c'=Uc$ and $\phi'=U\phi$ with $U^\dagger U=I$. Prove $(\phi')^\dagger c'=\phi^\dagger c$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Compute $(U\phi)^\dagger(Uc)=\phi^\dagger U^\dagger U c$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Interpret as basis-independence of $\langle\phi|\psi\rangle$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
$(\phi')^\dagger c'=(U\phi)^\dagger(Uc)=\phi^\dagger U^\dagger U c=\phi^\dagger c$.
\end{document}
```

## **C2 ‚Äî Similarity transform of operator matrices**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L05-C2 Operator transforms under basis change ‚Äî Problem}
Assume coefficient vectors transform as $c'=Uc$ when switching from basis $|n\rangle$ to $|\alpha\rangle$.
Show that the matrix representing the same operator satisfies $A' = UAU^\dagger$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Require that applying the operator then changing basis equals changing basis then applying the new matrix:
$c'_{\text{out}} = U(Ac)$ and also $c'_{\text{out}} = A'(Uc)$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Use equality for all $c$ to deduce $UA = A'U$ and hence $A'=UAU^\dagger$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
We demand representation consistency:
\[
c'_{\text{out}} = U(Ac) \quad\text{and}\quad c'_{\text{out}} = A'(Uc).
\]
Thus for all $c$, $UA c = A'U c$, so $UA = A'U$.
Multiply on the right by $U^\dagger$: $UAU^\dagger = A'(UU^\dagger)=A'$.
\end{document}
```

## **C3 ‚Äî Parseval identity (discrete and continuous)**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb,physics}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L05-C3 Parseval identities ‚Äî Problem}
Show (i) $\langle\psi|\psi\rangle=\sum_n|\langle n|\psi\rangle|^2$ and (ii) $\langle\psi|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,|\psi(x)|^2$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Insert discrete identity and continuous identity.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Interpret both as ‚Äútotal probability = 1‚Äù in different measurement contexts.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
(i) $\langle\psi|\psi\rangle=\langle\psi|(\sum_n|n\rangle\langle n|)|\psi\rangle=\sum_n|\langle n|\psi\rangle|^2$.
(ii) similarly $\langle\psi|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,\langle\psi|x\rangle\langle x|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,|\psi(x)|^2$.
\end{document}
```

## **C4 ‚Äî Kernel unitarity condition**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L05-C4 Transformation kernel orthonormality ‚Äî Problem}
Let $K(x,n)=\langle x|n\rangle$. Show that completeness and orthonormality imply
\[
\int dx\,K^*(x,m)K(x,n)=\delta_{mn}.
\]

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Start from $\delta_{mn}=\langle m|n\rangle$.
\item Insert $I=\int dx\,|x\rangle\langle x|$ between $\langle m|$ and $|n\rangle$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Recognize this as ‚Äúcolumns of the transformation are orthonormal‚Äù in the continuous sense.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
\[
\delta_{mn}=\langle m|n\rangle=\int dx\,\langle m|x\rangle\langle x|n\rangle
=\int dx\,K^*(x,m)K(x,n).
\]
\end{document}
```

## **C5 ‚Äî Structured essay: rigor of $$|x\rangle$$ and kernels**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L05-C5 Rigor essay ‚Äî Problem}
Write a 1--2 page structured essay:
\begin{enumerate}
\item Why is $|x\rangle$ a ``generalized'' eigenvector rather than an element of $\mathcal H$?
\item What does it mean to treat $A(x,x')$ as a kernel?
\item Which manipulations in this lecture are formal and which are rigorous in $L^2(\mathbb R)$?
\end{enumerate}

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Mention delta-normalization and distributions.
\item Keep it conceptual; no measure theory required.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Preview rigged Hilbert space: $\Phi\subset\mathcal H\subset\Phi'$.
\item Connect to why Lecture 12 exists.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution (model outline)}
A good answer should state:
\begin{itemize}
\item $|x\rangle$ is not square-integrable; it is delta-normalized and lives as a distributional object.
\item Kernels encode operator action via integral transforms; bounded operators yield well-defined integral kernels in many contexts.
\item Formal steps become rigorous in the framework of distributions / rigged Hilbert spaces; in $L^2$ the wavefunction is the true vector, and $|x\rangle$ is a generalized basis.
\end{itemize}
\end{document}
```

# **Lecture 6 ‚Äî Continuous Bases: $$|x\rangle$$, $$|p\rangle$$, Delta Functions, Fourier Transform**

### Dirac (abstract) ‚Üî Matrix/Kernel ‚Üî Wavefunction representations (fully unified)

## 90‚Äëminute pacing

*   **0‚Äì15:** Why continuous bases are ‚Äúgeneralized‚Äù; measurement with continuous outcomes
*   **15‚Äì35:** Position basis: $$\langle x|x'\rangle=\delta(x-x')$$, $$\int |x\rangle\langle x|dx=\mathbb I$$
*   **35‚Äì55:** Momentum basis and overlap $$\langle x|p\rangle$$; derive Fourier transform relations
*   **55‚Äì75:** Operator representations: $$\hat x$$ multiplication, $$\hat p=-i\hbar\partial_x$$
*   **75‚Äì90:** Kernels $$A(x,x')$$, expectation values, commutator preview $$[\hat x,\hat p]=i\hbar$$

## Core outcomes

Students can:

1.  Use continuous completeness to expand kets and compute inner products
2.  Interpret $$\psi(x)=\langle x|\psi\rangle$$ and $$\phi(p)=\langle p|\psi\rangle$$ as coordinate representations
3.  Derive Fourier transform relation using $$\langle x|p\rangle$$
4.  Represent operators $$x$$ and $$p$$ in the $$x$$-representation
5.  Compute expectation values in integral form and identify where delta/distributions are formal

# A) Reference anchors, historical anchors, expansion hooks

## Reference anchors (core)

*   **Dirac:** *The Principles of Quantum Mechanics* ‚Äî generalized eigenkets, delta normalization, transformation theory
*   **Sakurai & Napolitano:** *Modern Quantum Mechanics* ‚Äî continuous spectra, $$x/p$$ representations, Fourier relations

## Tiered references (suggested)

*   **HS:** concept-only: continuous outcomes, probability density vs probability
*   **BegUG:** Fourier transform basics; integrals; distributions at ‚Äúdelta as sifting‚Äù level
*   **AdvUG:** careful delta manipulations; normalization conventions; operator kernels
*   **MSc:** distributions formally; transformation kernels; Plancherel theorem intuition
*   **PhD:** rigged Hilbert space; unbounded operators and domains

## Historical anchors (for narrative/reading prompts)

*   **Heisenberg (1925):** observables and transition structures (matrix mechanics)
*   **Schr√∂dinger (1926):** wave mechanics and $$\psi(x)$$
*   **Dirac (1927):** transformation theory ($$\langle x|p\rangle$$ as kernel)
*   **von Neumann (1932):** continuous spectra rigor and operator foundations

## Expansion hooks

*   Momentum operator and translations ‚Üí Lecture 8 (time evolution) and Lecture 10 (rotations/spin)
*   Continuous spectra rigor ‚Üí Lecture 12 (rigged Hilbert spaces)
*   Commutators and uncertainty ‚Üí Lecture 7

***

# B) Learning tiers (Lecture 6 add-ons)

## HS

*   Probability density $$|\psi(x)|^2$$ vs probability in an interval
*   ‚ÄúContinuous outcomes‚Äù intuition (no delta formalism)

## BegUG

*   Delta function as ‚Äúsifting‚Äù: $$\int f(x)\delta(x-a)\,dx=f(a)$$
*   Fourier transform basics

## AdvUG

*   Derive $$\hat p=-i\hbar\partial_x$$ from $$\langle x|p\rangle$$
*   Understand normalization conventions $$\langle x|x'\rangle=\delta(x-x')$$

## MSc

*   Plancherel/Parseval as unitarity of Fourier transform
*   Kernel viewpoint: transformations are integral operators

## PhD

*   Domains of $$x$$ and $$p$$; generalized eigenvectors $$|x\rangle,|p\rangle\notin\mathcal H$$
*   Rigged Hilbert space preview: $$\Phi\subset \mathcal H\subset \Phi'$$

# C) Lecture notes (Narrative + derivations) ‚Äî LaTeX sources

## C1) Single-source chapter with instructor toggle

Copy as `L06_chapter.tex`

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}
\usepackage{geometry}
\geometry{margin=1in}
\usepackage{amsmath,amssymb,physics,hyperref}
\usepackage{enumitem}
\usepackage{tcolorbox}
\usepackage{booktabs}

\newif\ifinstructor

\newtcolorbox{pacingbox}{colback=blue!3!white,colframe=blue!60!black,title=90-minute pacing}
\newtcolorbox{outcomesbox}{colback=green!3!white,colframe=green!50!black,title=Core outcomes}
\newtcolorbox{warnbox}{colback=red!2!white,colframe=red!60!black,title=Common pitfalls}
\newtcolorbox{mapbox}{colback=purple!2!white,colframe=purple!60!black,title=Unified dictionary: Dirac $\leftrightarrow$ Wavefunctions $\leftrightarrow$ Kernels}

\title{Lecture 6: Continuous Bases, Delta Functions, and Fourier Transform}
\author{}
\date{}

\begin{document}
\maketitle

\begin{pacingbox}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
\item 0--15: Continuous outcomes and generalized bases
\item 15--35: Position basis: $\langle x|x'\rangle=\delta(x-x')$, $\int |x\rangle\langle x|dx=I$
\item 35--55: Momentum basis and $\langle x|p\rangle$; Fourier transform relations
\item 55--75: Operator representations: $\hat x$ as multiplication, $\hat p=-i\hbar\partial_x$
\item 75--90: Kernels $A(x,x')$; expectation values; commutator preview
\end{itemize}
\end{pacingbox}

\begin{outcomesbox}
\begin{enumerate}[leftmargin=*]
\item Use $\int dx\,|x\rangle\langle x|=I$ to derive $\psi(x)=\langle x|\psi\rangle$ and inner products.
\item Derive Fourier transform between $\psi(x)$ and $\phi(p)=\langle p|\psi\rangle$ from $\langle x|p\rangle$.
\item Derive $\hat p=-i\hbar\partial_x$ in the $x$-representation and compute expectation values.
\end{enumerate}
\end{outcomesbox}

\section{Continuous outcomes and generalized bases}
In many measurements (e.g. position), outcomes are continuous. We model this by a continuum of kets $|x\rangle$.
These kets are \emph{generalized} eigenstates: they are not normalizable in the usual sense, and their overlaps
involve the Dirac delta distribution.

\begin{warnbox}
$|x\rangle$ is not a normal element of $\mathcal H$ (it is delta-normalized). Treat it as a formal tool whose
consistent use is justified later (rigged Hilbert spaces).
\end{warnbox}

\section{Position basis}
Postulate (formal):
\[
\langle x|x'\rangle=\delta(x-x'),\qquad \int_{-\infty}^{\infty} dx\,|x\rangle\langle x| = I.
\]
Define the wavefunction:
\[
\psi(x)=\langle x|\psi\rangle.
\]
Then expansion follows by inserting identity:
\[
|\psi\rangle = \int dx\,|x\rangle\langle x|\psi\rangle = \int dx\,|x\rangle\,\psi(x).
\]

\subsection{Inner product}
\[
\langle\phi|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,\langle\phi|x\rangle\langle x|\psi\rangle
=\int dx\,\phi^*(x)\psi(x).
\]

\section{Momentum basis and Fourier transform}
Similarly define momentum kets $|p\rangle$ with
\[
\langle p|p'\rangle=\delta(p-p'),\qquad \int dp\,|p\rangle\langle p|=I,\qquad \phi(p)=\langle p|\psi\rangle.
\]
Choose the standard convention:
\[
\langle x|p\rangle = \frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi\hbar}}e^{ipx/\hbar}.
\]
Insert the momentum identity to relate representations:
\[
\psi(x)=\langle x|\psi\rangle=\int dp\,\langle x|p\rangle\langle p|\psi\rangle
=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi\hbar}}\int dp\,e^{ipx/\hbar}\phi(p).
\]
Similarly,
\[
\phi(p)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi\hbar}}\int dx\,e^{-ipx/\hbar}\psi(x).
\]
Thus the change of basis between $x$ and $p$ is a Fourier transform.

\section{Operators in the $x$-representation}
\subsection{Position operator}
Because $\hat x|x\rangle = x|x\rangle$, we get
\[
(\hat x\psi)(x)=\langle x|\hat x|\psi\rangle = x\langle x|\psi\rangle = x\psi(x).
\]

\subsection{Momentum operator}
Because $\hat p|p\rangle = p|p\rangle$, we compute
\[
\langle x|\hat p|\psi\rangle = \int dp\,\langle x|p\rangle\,p\,\phi(p).
\]
Using $\langle x|p\rangle\propto e^{ipx/\hbar}$, note that $p e^{ipx/\hbar} = -i\hbar\,\partial_x e^{ipx/\hbar}$.
Move $-i\hbar\partial_x$ outside the integral (formal):
\[
(\hat p\psi)(x) = -i\hbar\,\frac{d}{dx}\psi(x).
\]

\section{Kernels and expectation values}
Define the kernel of an operator:
\[
A(x,x')=\langle x|\hat A|x'\rangle.
\]
Then
\[
(\hat A\psi)(x)=\int dx'\,A(x,x')\psi(x').
\]
Expectation value:
\[
\langle\hat A\rangle=\langle\psi|\hat A|\psi\rangle = \int dx\,dx'\,\psi^*(x)A(x,x')\psi(x').
\]
For $\hat x$, the kernel is $x\delta(x-x')$; for $\hat p$, it is $-i\hbar\,\partial_x\delta(x-x')$ (formal).

\begin{mapbox}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Dirac} & \textbf{$x$-rep} & \textbf{$p$-rep}\\ \midrule
$\psi(x)=\langle x|\psi\rangle$ & wavefunction & $\phi(p)=\langle p|\psi\rangle$\\
$I=\int dx\,|x\rangle\langle x|$ & completeness & $I=\int dp\,|p\rangle\langle p|$\\
$\langle x|p\rangle$ & kernel & Fourier phase\\
$\hat x$ & $(x\psi)(x)$ & $i\hbar\,\partial_p\phi(p)$ (preview)\\
$\hat p$ & $-i\hbar\partial_x\psi(x)$ & $(p\phi)(p)$\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{mapbox}

\ifinstructor
\appendix
\section{Instructor-only notes}
Emphasize that delta-normalized kets are formal objects; highlight where integration by parts is used to derive
$\hat p=-i\hbar\partial_x$ and note boundary conditions assumptions. Preview commutator $[\hat x,\hat p]=i\hbar$
and uncertainty (Lecture 7).
\fi

\end{document}
```

```latex
\documentclass{beamer}
\usetheme{Madrid}
\usepackage{amsmath}
\title{Lecture 6: Continuous Bases and Fourier Transform}
\begin{document}

\begin{frame}\titlepage\end{frame}

\begin{frame}{Position basis}
\[
\langle x|x'\rangle=\delta(x-x'),\qquad \int dx\,|x\rangle\langle x|=I
\]
\[
\psi(x)=\langle x|\psi\rangle,\qquad |\psi\rangle=\int dx\,|x\rangle\psi(x)
\]
\end{frame}

\begin{frame}{Momentum basis and overlap}
\[
\langle x|p\rangle=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi\hbar}}e^{ipx/\hbar}
\]
\[
\psi(x)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi\hbar}}\int dp\,e^{ipx/\hbar}\phi(p)
\]
\end{frame}

\begin{frame}{Operators}
\[
(\hat x\psi)(x)=x\psi(x),\qquad (\hat p\psi)(x)=-i\hbar\frac{d}{dx}\psi(x)
\]
\end{frame}

\begin{frame}{Kernel form}
\[
A(x,x')=\langle x|\hat A|x'\rangle,\qquad (A\psi)(x)=\int dx'\,A(x,x')\psi(x')
\]
\end{frame}

\end{document}
```

***

# E) Concept Questions (CQ) ‚Äî 10

1.  Why is position measurement modeled by a continuous basis?
2.  What does $$\delta(x-x')$$ mean operationally (sifting)?
3.  Why can‚Äôt $$|x\rangle$$ be normalized like discrete basis vectors?
4.  What is $$\psi(x)$$ in Dirac language?
5.  What does completeness $$\int |x\rangle\langle x|dx=I$$ accomplish?
6.  Why is $$\langle x|p\rangle$$ an exponential?
7.  How does the Fourier transform arise as a basis change?
8.  Why does $$\hat x$$ act by multiplication in the $$x$$-representation?
9.  How do we derive $$\hat p=-i\hbar\partial_x$$ and what assumptions enter?
10. What is an operator kernel $$A(x,x')$$ and why is it useful?

***

# F) **Simple Problem Set (SPS) ‚Äî 10**

**S1** Use $$\int|x\rangle\langle x|dx=I$$ to derive $$|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,|x\rangle\psi(x)$$  
**S2** Derive $$\langle\phi|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,\phi^*(x)\psi(x)$$  
**S3** Prove ‚Äúsifting‚Äù identity $$\int dx\,f(x)\delta(x-a)=f(a)$$ (formal)  
**S4** Show $$\int dx\,\delta(x-x')g(x)=g(x')$$  
**S5** Given $$\langle x|p\rangle=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi\hbar}}e^{ipx/\hbar}$$, derive Fourier pair between $$\psi(x)$$ and $$\phi(p)$$  
**S6** Verify normalization consistency: if $$\int dx|\psi(x)|^2=1$$, then $$\int dp|\phi(p)|^2=1$$ (use Parseval result stated; proof in CPS)  
**S7** Show $$(\hat x\psi)(x)=x\psi(x)$$  
**S8** Derive $$(\hat p\psi)(x)=-i\hbar\partial_x\psi(x)$$ from $$\langle x|p\rangle$$  
**S9** Show kernel action: $$(A\psi)(x)=\int dx'\,A(x,x')\psi(x')$$  
**S10** Compute $$\langle x\rangle=\int dx\,x|\psi(x)|^2$$ and $$\langle p\rangle=\int dp\,p|\phi(p)|^2$$ for a given example

***

# G) **Complex Problem Set (CPS) ‚Äî 5**

**C1** Prove Parseval/Plancherel for the chosen $$\langle x|p\rangle$$ normalization: $$\int | \psi(x)|^2dx=\int |\phi(p)|^2dp$$  
**C2** Derive $$\langle x|p\rangle$$ normalization by enforcing $$\langle p|p'\rangle=\delta(p-p')$$  
**C3** Prove $$[\hat x,\hat p]=i\hbar$$ acting on a suitable class of wavefunctions  
**C4** Show translation operator $$T(a)=e^{-ia\hat p/\hbar}$$ satisfies $$(T(a)\psi)(x)=\psi(x-a)$$ (formal)  
**C5 (MSc/PhD)** Structured essay: what is ‚Äúrigor‚Äù behind $$|x\rangle$$, delta functions, and integration by parts assumptions?

***

# H) Projects

## Simple Project (SPJ): ‚ÄúFourier Transform Lab‚Äù

*   Choose 3 normalized wavefunctions (Gaussian, box, superposition of Gaussians)
*   Numerically compute Fourier transform to momentum space
*   Plot $$|\psi(x)|^2$$ and $$|\phi(p)|^2$$; verify normalization

Deliverables: code + plots + 2-page explanation.

## Complex Project (CPJ): ‚ÄúOperator representations and kernels‚Äù

*   Implement $$\hat x$$ and $$\hat p$$ in $$x$$-space
*   Verify commutator numerically on test functions
*   Construct kernels $$x\delta(x-x')$$ and $$-i\hbar\partial_x\delta(x-x')$$ in discrete approximation and compare actions

Deliverables: 8‚Äì12 page report + appendix.

# I) Research questions

## Well-defined (WRQ)

**How did Dirac‚Äôs transformation theory explain the equivalence of Schr√∂dinger wave mechanics and operator/matrix methods for continuous variables?**  
(4‚Äì6 pages; must include explanation of $$\langle x|p\rangle$$ as a transformation kernel)

## Open-ended (ORQ)

**Can the canonical commutation relation $$[\hat x,\hat p]=i\hbar$$ be derived purely from operational measurement assumptions?**  
Write a proposal with assumptions and consequences.

# K) Exercise packets ‚Äî **all 15 problems** (10 SPS + 5 CPS)

Each packet below is a complete mini-document: **Problem ‚Üí Suggestions ‚Üí Advanced ‚Üí Detailed solution**.

> Copy each block into separate files `L06_S1.tex` ‚Ä¶ `L06_C5.tex` as desired.

## **S1 ‚Äî Expand ket in position basis**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb,physics}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L06-S1 Expansion in $x$-basis ‚Äî Problem}
Assume $\int dx\,|x\rangle\langle x|=I$. Define $\psi(x)=\langle x|\psi\rangle$ and show
$|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,|x\rangle\psi(x)$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Insert the identity in front of $|\psi\rangle$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Interpret $\psi(x)$ as the coordinate of the abstract ket in the $x$ basis.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
$|\psi\rangle=I|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,|x\rangle\langle x|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,|x\rangle\psi(x)$.
\end{document}
```

## **S2 ‚Äî Inner product as an integral**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb,physics}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L06-S2 Inner product ‚Äî Problem}
Assume $\int dx\,|x\rangle\langle x|=I$. Show $\langle\phi|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,\phi^*(x)\psi(x)$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Insert the identity between $\langle\phi|$ and $|\psi\rangle$.
\item Use $\langle\phi|x\rangle=\phi^*(x)$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Compare to discrete formula $\sum_n \phi_n^*\psi_n$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
$\langle\phi|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,\langle\phi|x\rangle\langle x|\psi\rangle=\int dx\,\phi^*(x)\psi(x)$.
\end{document}
```

## **S3 ‚Äî Delta ‚Äúsifting‚Äù**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L06-S3 Sifting ‚Äî Problem}
Assuming the sifting property of $\delta$, evaluate $\int dx\,f(x)\delta(x-a)$ and state the result.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Recall $\delta(x-a)$ ``picks out'' the value at $x=a$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Mention that $\delta$ is a distribution, not an ordinary function.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
By definition of the Dirac delta distribution,
\[
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty} f(x)\delta(x-a)\,dx=f(a).
\]
\end{document}
```

## **S4 ‚Äî Delta with shifted argument**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L06-S4 Delta action ‚Äî Problem}
Evaluate $\int dx\,\delta(x-x')g(x)$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Treat $x'$ as a constant; apply sifting.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Explain why this is the continuum analog of $\sum_n \delta_{nn'}g_n=g_{n'}$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
\[
\int dx\,\delta(x-x')g(x)=g(x').
\]
\end{document}
```

## **S5 ‚Äî Fourier relation from $$\langle x|p\rangle$$**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb,physics}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L06-S5 Fourier transform ‚Äî Problem}
Assume $\langle x|p\rangle=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi\hbar}}e^{ipx/\hbar}$ and $I=\int dp\,|p\rangle\langle p|$.
Show $\psi(x)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi\hbar}}\int dp\,e^{ipx/\hbar}\phi(p)$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Insert $I$ in $\psi(x)=\langle x|\psi\rangle$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Identify $\phi(p)=\langle p|\psi\rangle$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
\[
\psi(x)=\langle x|\psi\rangle=\int dp\,\langle x|p\rangle\langle p|\psi\rangle
=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi\hbar}}\int dp\,e^{ipx/\hbar}\phi(p).
\]
\end{document}
```

## **S6 ‚Äî Normalization consistency (stated)**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L06-S6 Norm consistency ‚Äî Problem}
Assume Parseval/Plancherel holds for the chosen normalization. Show that if $\int dx|\psi(x)|^2=1$ then $\int dp|\phi(p)|^2=1$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Use $\int dx|\psi(x)|^2=\int dp|\phi(p)|^2$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Note: the proof is asked in C1.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
By Parseval/Plancherel, $\int dx|\psi(x)|^2=\int dp|\phi(p)|^2$. If the left side equals 1, the right side equals 1.
\end{document}
```

## **S7 ‚Äî $$\hat x$$ acts by multiplication**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb,physics}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L06-S7 Position operator ‚Äî Problem}
Using $\hat x|x\rangle=x|x\rangle$, show $(\hat x\psi)(x)=x\psi(x)$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Start from $(\hat x\psi)(x)=\langle x|\hat x|\psi\rangle$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Insert $I=\int dx'|x'\rangle\langle x'|$ if needed.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
\[
(\hat x\psi)(x)=\langle x|\hat x|\psi\rangle=\langle x|x|\psi\rangle=x\langle x|\psi\rangle=x\psi(x).
\]
\end{document}
```

## **S8 ‚Äî Derive $$\hat p=-i\hbar\partial_x$$**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb,physics}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L06-S8 Momentum operator ‚Äî Problem}
Assume $\langle x|p\rangle=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi\hbar}}e^{ipx/\hbar}$ and $\phi(p)=\langle p|\psi\rangle$.
Show $(\hat p\psi)(x)=-i\hbar\,\partial_x\psi(x)$ (formal).

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Write $(\hat p\psi)(x)=\langle x|\hat p|\psi\rangle=\int dp\,\langle x|p\rangle\,p\,\phi(p)$.
\item Use $p e^{ipx/\hbar}=-i\hbar \partial_x e^{ipx/\hbar}$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Move $\partial_x$ outside the integral and recognize the remaining integral as $\psi(x)$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
\[
(\hat p\psi)(x)=\int dp\,\langle x|p\rangle\,p\,\phi(p)
=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi\hbar}}\int dp\,p\,e^{ipx/\hbar}\phi(p).
\]
Since $p e^{ipx/\hbar}=-i\hbar\partial_x e^{ipx/\hbar}$,
\[
(\hat p\psi)(x)= -i\hbar\,\partial_x\left(\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi\hbar}}\int dp\,e^{ipx/\hbar}\phi(p)\right)
=-i\hbar\,\partial_x\psi(x).
\]
\end{document}
```

## **S9 ‚Äî Kernel action**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb,physics}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L06-S9 Kernel action ‚Äî Problem}
Let $A(x,x')=\langle x|\hat A|x'\rangle$. Show $(A\psi)(x)=\int dx'\,A(x,x')\psi(x')$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Start from $(A\psi)(x)=\langle x|\hat A|\psi\rangle$.
\item Insert $I=\int dx'|x'\rangle\langle x'|$ after $\hat A$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Relate to discrete formula $c'_m=\sum_n A_{mn}c_n$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
\[
(A\psi)(x)=\langle x|\hat A|\psi\rangle=\int dx'\,\langle x|\hat A|x'\rangle\langle x'|\psi\rangle
=\int dx'\,A(x,x')\psi(x').
\]
\end{document}
```

## **S10 ‚Äî Expectation values in $$x$$ and $$p$$**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L06-S10 Expectations ‚Äî Problem}
State the formulas for $\langle x\rangle$ and $\langle p\rangle$ in terms of $\psi(x)$ and $\phi(p)$, respectively.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Use probability densities $|\psi(x)|^2$ and $|\phi(p)|^2$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Mention assumptions: normalized states and standard Born rule.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
\[
\langle x\rangle=\int dx\,x|\psi(x)|^2,\qquad \langle p\rangle=\int dp\,p|\phi(p)|^2.
\]
\end{document}
```

***

## **C1 ‚Äî Parseval/Plancherel proof**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L06-C1 Parseval/Plancherel ‚Äî Problem}
With $\psi(x)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi\hbar}}\int dp\,e^{ipx/\hbar}\phi(p)$ and
$\phi(p)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi\hbar}}\int dx\,e^{-ipx/\hbar}\psi(x)$, prove
\[
\int dx\,|\psi(x)|^2=\int dp\,|\phi(p)|^2.
\]

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Write $\int dx\,\psi^*(x)\psi(x)$ and substitute the Fourier forms.
\item Use $\int dx\,e^{i(p-p')x/\hbar}=2\pi\hbar\,\delta(p-p')$ (distribution identity).
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Keep track of constants carefully; they cancel with $1/(2\pi\hbar)$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
Start:
\[
\int dx\,|\psi(x)|^2=\int dx\,\psi^*(x)\psi(x).
\]
Insert Fourier forms:
\[
\psi(x)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi\hbar}}\int dp\,e^{ipx/\hbar}\phi(p),\quad
\psi^*(x)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi\hbar}}\int dp'\,e^{-ip'x/\hbar}\phi^*(p').
\]
Thus
\[
\int dx\,|\psi(x)|^2=\frac{1}{2\pi\hbar}\int dp\,dp'\,\phi^*(p')\phi(p)\int dx\,e^{i(p-p')x/\hbar}.
\]
Use $\int dx\,e^{i(p-p')x/\hbar}=2\pi\hbar\,\delta(p-p')$:
\[
\int dx\,|\psi(x)|^2=\int dp\,dp'\,\phi^*(p')\phi(p)\delta(p-p')=\int dp\,|\phi(p)|^2.
\]
\end{document}
```

## **C2 ‚Äî Normalize $$\langle x|p\rangle$$**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L06-C2 Normalization of $\langle x|p\rangle$ ‚Äî Problem}
Assume $\langle x|p\rangle=C\,e^{ipx/\hbar}$. Determine $C$ by requiring $\langle p|p'\rangle=\delta(p-p')$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Use $\langle p|p'\rangle=\int dx\,\langle p|x\rangle\langle x|p'\rangle$.
\item Note $\langle p|x\rangle=\langle x|p\rangle^*$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Use $\int dx\,e^{i(p'-p)x/\hbar}=2\pi\hbar\,\delta(p'-p)$.
\item Solve $|C|^2(2\pi\hbar)=1$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
Compute
\[
\langle p|p'\rangle=\int dx\,\langle p|x\rangle\langle x|p'\rangle
=\int dx\,C^*e^{-ipx/\hbar}\,C e^{ip'x/\hbar}
=|C|^2\int dx\,e^{i(p'-p)x/\hbar}.
\]
Using $\int dx\,e^{i(p'-p)x/\hbar}=2\pi\hbar\,\delta(p'-p)$ gives
\[
\langle p|p'\rangle = |C|^2(2\pi\hbar)\delta(p'-p).
\]
To match $\delta(p'-p)$, require $|C|^2(2\pi\hbar)=1$, hence
\[
C=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi\hbar}} \quad \text{(choose positive real)}.
\]
\end{document}
```

## **C3 ‚Äî Commutator $$[\hat x,\hat p]=i\hbar$$**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L06-C3 Canonical commutator ‚Äî Problem}
Using $(\hat x\psi)(x)=x\psi(x)$ and $(\hat p\psi)(x)=-i\hbar\partial_x\psi(x)$, show
\[
([\hat x,\hat p]\psi)(x)=i\hbar\,\psi(x)
\]
for sufficiently smooth $\psi$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Compute $(\hat x\hat p\psi)(x)$ and $(\hat p\hat x\psi)(x)$.
\item Subtract.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Use product rule: $\partial_x(x\psi)=\psi+x\partial_x\psi$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
Compute:
\[
(\hat x\hat p\psi)(x)=x(-i\hbar\partial_x\psi(x))=-i\hbar x\psi'(x).
\]
Next
\[
(\hat p\hat x\psi)(x)=-i\hbar\partial_x(x\psi(x))=-i\hbar(\psi(x)+x\psi'(x)).
\]
Subtract:
\[
([\hat x,\hat p]\psi)(x)=(\hat x\hat p-\hat p\hat x)\psi
=-i\hbar x\psi'(x)-\big[-i\hbar(\psi+x\psi')\big]=i\hbar\psi(x).
\]
\end{document}
```

## **C4 ‚Äî Translation operator acts as shift**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L06-C4 Translation operator ‚Äî Problem}
Let $T(a)=e^{-ia\hat p/\hbar}$. Show formally that $(T(a)\psi)(x)=\psi(x-a)$.

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Use $\hat p=-i\hbar\partial_x$ so $-ia\hat p/\hbar = a\partial_x$.
\item Recall $e^{a\partial_x}f(x)=f(x+a)$ (Taylor series).
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}\begin{itemize}
\item Expand $T(a)$ as a power series and apply to $\psi$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution}
Using $\hat p=-i\hbar\partial_x$,
\[
T(a)=e^{-ia\hat p/\hbar}=e^{a\partial_x}.
\]
Apply as a series:
\[
(e^{a\partial_x}\psi)(x)=\sum_{n=0}^\infty \frac{a^n}{n!}\partial_x^n\psi(x)=\psi(x+a)
\]
(by Taylor‚Äôs theorem). With sign conventions, this yields the shift $(T(a)\psi)(x)=\psi(x-a)$ depending on the chosen exponent sign; with $e^{-ia\hat p/\hbar}$ the shift is to the right by $a$: $\psi(x-a)$.
\end{document}
```

## **C5 ‚Äî Essay on rigor**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}\usepackage{geometry}\geometry{margin=1in}\begin{document}
\section*{L06-C5 Rigor and generalized kets ‚Äî Problem}
Write a 1--2 page structured essay:
\begin{enumerate}
\item Why are $|x\rangle$ and $|p\rangle$ not normalizable in $\mathcal H$?
\item Where did we use ``formal'' steps (e.g., moving derivatives outside integrals)?
\item What assumptions ensure boundary terms vanish when deriving $\hat p=-i\hbar\partial_x$?
\end{enumerate}

\newpage\section*{Suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Mention delta-normalization and distributions.
\item Mention smoothness/decay assumptions on $\psi$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Advanced suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Preview rigged Hilbert space: $\Phi\subset\mathcal H\subset\Phi'$.
\item Mention domains of unbounded operators.
\end{itemize}

\newpage\section*{Detailed solution (model outline)}
A good answer states:
\begin{itemize}
\item $|x\rangle$ and $|p\rangle$ correspond to delta-normalized objects; not square-integrable, so not in $\mathcal H=L^2(\mathbb R)$.
\item The derivation of $\hat p=-i\hbar\partial_x$ uses distributional identities and exchanging differentiation/integration.
\item Boundary terms vanish if $\psi$ decays sufficiently fast or satisfies appropriate boundary conditions; these are domain assumptions.
\item Rigged Hilbert spaces provide a framework where $|x\rangle$ lives as a continuous linear functional.
\end{itemize}
\end{document}
```

# **Lecture 7 ‚Äî Measurement Theory, Compatibility, Uncertainty + POVM Preview**

### Projective measurements (PVM) + L√ºders rule + POVM/Kraus preview

## 90‚Äëminute pacing

*   **0‚Äì15:** Measurement as state update; repeatability; L√ºders recap
*   **15‚Äì35:** Compatibility and commutators; joint measurability (projective case)
*   **35‚Äì60:** Variance, uncertainty; derive Robertson inequality
*   **60‚Äì75:** Schr√∂dinger (strengthened) uncertainty; covariance term
*   **75‚Äì90:** POVM preview: effects $$E_i$$, Kraus operators $$M_i$$, generalized update; examples

## Core outcomes

Students can:

1.  Compute probabilities and post-measurement states for **projective measurements** (including degeneracy)
2.  Use commutators to discuss **compatibility** and derive **uncertainty bounds**
3.  Distinguish **PVM** (projectors) from **POVM** (positive effects) and compute POVM statistics
4.  Use Kraus operators to compute both probabilities and state updates (preview level)
5.  Explain what is operationally meant by ‚Äúmeasurement disturbance‚Äù and why POVMs broaden measurement models

# C) Lecture notes (Narrative + derivations) ‚Äî LaTeX sources

## C1) Single-source chapter with instructor toggle

Copy as `L07_chapter.tex`

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}
\usepackage{geometry}
\geometry{margin=1in}
\usepackage{amsmath,amssymb,physics,hyperref}
\usepackage{enumitem}
\usepackage{tcolorbox}
\usepackage{booktabs}

\newif\ifinstructor

\newtcolorbox{pacingbox}{colback=blue!3!white,colframe=blue!60!black,title=90-minute pacing}
\newtcolorbox{outcomesbox}{colback=green!3!white,colframe=green!50!black,title=Core outcomes}
\newtcolorbox{warnbox}{colback=red!2!white,colframe=red!60!black,title=Common pitfalls}
\newtcolorbox{mapbox}{colback=purple!2!white,colframe=purple!60!black,title=PVM/L\"uders $\leftrightarrow$ POVM/Kraus preview}

\title{Lecture 7: Measurement, Compatibility, Uncertainty + POVM Preview}
\author{}
\date{}

\begin{document}
\maketitle

\begin{pacingbox}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
\item 0--15: Projective measurement and L\"uders update (recap)
\item 15--35: Compatibility, commutators, joint measurability (projective case)
\item 35--60: Variance and Robertson uncertainty (derivation)
\item 60--75: Schr\"odinger uncertainty (covariance term)
\item 75--90: POVM preview: effects $E_i$, Kraus operators $M_i$, generalized update
\end{itemize}
\end{pacingbox}

\begin{outcomesbox}
\begin{enumerate}[leftmargin=*]
\item Compute projective measurement probabilities $p(a)=\langle\psi|P_a|\psi\rangle$ and L\"uders-updated states.
\item Derive Robertson (and Schr\"odinger) uncertainty relations from operator inequalities.
\item Compute POVM probabilities $p(i)=\langle\psi|E_i|\psi\rangle$ and (preview) Kraus updates.
\end{enumerate}
\end{outcomesbox}

\section{Projective measurements (PVM) and L\"uders rule}
A projective measurement of $A$ is described by orthogonal projectors $\{P_a\}$ with
$P_aP_b=\delta_{ab}P_a$ and $\sum_a P_a=I$ (degeneracy allowed: $P_a$ projects onto the eigenspace).

Probability of outcome $a$ in pure state $|\psi\rangle$:
\[
p(a)=\langle\psi|P_a|\psi\rangle.
\]
L\"uders state update (pure state):
\[
|\psi\rangle \mapsto \frac{P_a|\psi\rangle}{\sqrt{\langle\psi|P_a|\psi\rangle}}.
\]
Density-matrix form:
\[
\rho \mapsto \rho_a'=\frac{P_a\rho P_a}{\Tr(P_a\rho)}.
\]
If the outcome is ignored, the post-measurement state is
\[
\rho'=\sum_a P_a\rho P_a.
\]

\begin{warnbox}
For degenerate outcomes, collapsing to a specific eigenvector adds information not contained in the measurement.
L\"uders projects onto the eigenspace and preserves exactly what was learned.
\end{warnbox}

\section{Compatibility and commutators}
Two sharp (projective) observables $A$ and $B$ are compatible if they can be measured jointly without mutual
disturbance in the idealized sense. A sufficient condition (and in finite dimension essentially equivalent) is
\[
[\hat A,\hat B]=0,
\]
which implies they share a common eigenbasis (simultaneous diagonalization).

\section{Variance and uncertainty}
For an observable $\hat A$ in state $|\psi\rangle$ define
\[
\langle A\rangle=\langle\psi|\hat A|\psi\rangle,\qquad (\Delta A)^2=\langle (\hat A-\langle A\rangle)^2\rangle.
\]
Let $\Delta\hat A=\hat A-\langle A\rangle I$.

\subsection{Robertson uncertainty relation}
Consider the nonnegative norm
\[
\|(\Delta\hat A + i\lambda \Delta\hat B)|\psi\rangle\|^2\ge 0
\quad \text{for all real }\lambda.
\]
Expanding yields a quadratic in $\lambda$ whose discriminant must be nonpositive, giving
\[
\Delta A\,\Delta B \ge \frac12\,|\langle[\hat A,\hat B]\rangle|.
\]

\subsection{Schr\"odinger uncertainty relation}
A stronger inequality includes the covariance:
\[
(\Delta A)^2(\Delta B)^2 \ge \left(\frac12|\langle[\hat A,\hat B]\rangle|\right)^2
+ \left(\frac12\langle\{\Delta\hat A,\Delta\hat B\}\rangle\right)^2,
\]
where $\{X,Y\}=XY+YX$.

\section{POVM preview: generalized measurements}
Projective measurements are not the most general. A POVM is a set of positive operators (effects)
\[
E_i\ge 0,\qquad \sum_i E_i=I.
\]
Probabilities:
\[
p(i)=\langle\psi|E_i|\psi\rangle \quad (\text{or } p(i)=\Tr(\rho E_i)).
\]
Projective measurement is the special case $E_i=P_i$ with orthogonal projectors.

\subsection{Kraus operators and state update (instrument)}
Often a POVM arises from measurement operators $M_i$ (Kraus operators) such that
\[
E_i=M_i^\dagger M_i,\qquad \sum_i M_i^\dagger M_i=I.
\]
Then
\[
p(i)=\Tr(M_i\rho M_i^\dagger),
\qquad
\rho \mapsto \rho_i'=\frac{M_i\rho M_i^\dagger}{p(i)}.
\]
Ignoring outcomes gives a quantum channel:
\[
\rho'=\sum_i M_i\rho M_i^\dagger.
\]

\begin{mapbox}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Sharp (PVM)} & \textbf{General (POVM)} & \textbf{Update rule}\\ \midrule
$P_a$ projectors, $\sum_a P_a=I$ & $E_i\ge 0$, $\sum_i E_i=I$ & $|\psi\rangle\to P_a|\psi\rangle/\sqrt{p(a)}$\\
prob $p(a)=\langle\psi|P_a|\psi\rangle$ & prob $p(i)=\langle\psi|E_i|\psi\rangle$ & $\rho\to M_i\rho M_i^\dagger/p(i)$\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{mapbox}

\ifinstructor
\appendix
\section{Instructor-only notes}
Highlight: POVM extends what counts as a measurement; it may model coarse-graining, detector inefficiency,
or indirect measurements. Emphasize that compatibility/joint measurability is more subtle for POVMs than for PVMs
(we preview only).
\fi

\end{document}
```

## D1) Beamer deck (LaTeX) ‚Äî `L07_slides_beamer.tex`

```latex
\documentclass{beamer}
\usetheme{Madrid}
\usepackage{amsmath}
\title{Lecture 7: Measurement, Uncertainty, and POVM Preview}
\begin{document}

\begin{frame}\titlepage\end{frame}

\begin{frame}{Projective measurement (PVM) + L\"uders}
\[
p(a)=\langle\psi|P_a|\psi\rangle,\quad |\psi\rangle\to \frac{P_a|\psi\rangle}{\sqrt{p(a)}}
\]
\[
\rho\to \frac{P_a\rho P_a}{\Tr(P_a\rho)},\quad \rho'=\sum_a P_a\rho P_a
\]
\end{frame}

\begin{frame}{Compatibility}
\[
[A,B]=0 \ \Rightarrow\ \text{simultaneous diagonalization (finite-dim)}
\]
\end{frame}

\begin{frame}{Robertson uncertainty}
\[
\Delta A\,\Delta B \ge \frac12|\langle[A,B]\rangle|
\]
\end{frame}

\begin{frame}{Schr\"odinger uncertainty}
\[
(\Delta A)^2(\Delta B)^2 \ge \left(\frac12|\langle[A,B]\rangle|\right)^2
+\left(\frac12\langle\{\Delta A,\Delta B\}\rangle\right)^2
\]
\end{frame}

\begin{frame}{POVM preview}
\[
E_i\ge0,\ \sum_i E_i=I,\quad p(i)=\Tr(\rho E_i)
\]
Kraus form:
\[
E_i=M_i^\dagger M_i,\quad \rho\to \frac{M_i\rho M_i^\dagger}{p(i)}
\]
\end{frame}

\end{document}
```

# E) Concept Questions (CQ) ‚Äî 10

1.  What does L√ºders rule do differently in degenerate measurements?
2.  What does ‚Äúcompatibility‚Äù mean operationally for projective measurements?
3.  Why does $$[A,B]=0$$ matter?
4.  What is variance and why is it the right measure of spread?
5.  What is $$\Delta\hat A$$ and why do we subtract the mean?
6.  Outline (in words) why Robertson inequality comes from a nonnegative norm.
7.  What extra term appears in Schr√∂dinger uncertainty and what does it mean?
8.  What is a POVM and how is it more general than a projector-valued measurement?
9.  What are Kraus operators and what do they encode?
10. When might you need POVMs physically (coarse graining, inefficiency, indirect measurement)?

***

# F) **Simple Problem Set (SPS) ‚Äî 10**

S1 Compute variance $$\Delta A^2$$ for a 2√ó2 observable and state  
S2 Compute commutator $$[A,B]$$ for given 2√ó2 matrices  
S3 Check compatibility by finding a common eigenbasis when $$[A,B]=0$$ (2√ó2 case)  
S4 For Pauli observables, compute $$\Delta \sigma_x,\Delta \sigma_z$$ in a given qubit state  
S5 Compute Robertson lower bound for a qubit pair $$A=\sigma_x,B=\sigma_z$$  
S6 Projective measurement probability $$p(a)=\langle\psi|P_a|\psi\rangle$$ + L√ºders update  
S7 Degenerate L√ºders update with a given projector $$P_a$$ (3D example)  
S8 POVM probabilities: given effects $$E_1,E_2$$, compute $$p(1),p(2)$$ for $$|\psi\rangle$$  
S9 Kraus to POVM: given $$M_i$$, compute $$E_i=M_i^\dagger M_i$$ and $$p(i)$$  
S10 Show a PVM is a POVM: $$E_i=P_i$$ satisfies POVM conditions and matches Born rule

***

# G) **Complex Problem Set (CPS) ‚Äî 5**

C1 Derive Robertson uncertainty $$\Delta A\Delta B\ge\frac12|\langle[A,B]\rangle|$$  
C2 Derive Schr√∂dinger uncertainty (anticommutator/covariance term)  
C3 Show L√ºders update preserves normalization (pure and density matrix forms)  
C4 Show Kraus completeness $$\sum_i M_i^\dagger M_i=I$$ implies probabilities sum to 1 and defines a CPTP map when outcomes are ignored  
C5 (MSc/PhD) Naimark dilation preview (structured proof sketch): any POVM can be realized as a projective measurement on an enlarged space

# H) Projects

## Simple Project (SPJ): ‚ÄúMeasurement simulator‚Äù

Implement:

*   a PVM (projectors) and L√ºders update
*   a POVM (effects + Kraus operators) and its update  
    Run Monte Carlo trials to compare predicted frequencies to theory.

Deliverables: code + 3 experiments + brief report.

## Complex Project (CPJ): ‚ÄúUnsharp measurement vs disturbance‚Äù

Implement a qubit **unsharp POVM** (e.g. $$E_\pm=\frac12(I\pm \eta\sigma_z)$$, $$0\le\eta\le1$$) and explore:

*   outcome statistics vs $$\eta$$
*   post-measurement state purity/disturbance vs $$\eta$$
*   compare to sharp projective case $$\eta=1$$

Deliverables: 8‚Äì12 page report + plots + interpretation.

***

# I) Research questions

## Well-defined (WRQ)

**Why did L√ºders refine the projection postulate for degeneracy, and how does the POVM/Kraus framework generalize it?**  
(5‚Äì7 pages, include historical and technical discussion)

## Open-ended (ORQ)

**Can uncertainty relations be formulated as information‚Äìdisturbance tradeoffs for POVMs (beyond Robertson)?**  
Write a proposal with candidate definitions and how to test them.

***

## J1) Extra practice ‚Äî `L07_extra_practice.tex`

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}
\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb,physics}
\geometry{margin=1in}
\title{Lecture 7 ‚Äî Extra Practice}
\date{}
\begin{document}\maketitle

\section*{Practice A (PVM + L√ºders)}
\begin{enumerate}
\item For $P_0=|0\rangle\langle0|$ and $|\psi\rangle=\alpha|0\rangle+\beta|1\rangle$, compute $p(0)$ and post-state.
\item For a 3D space with $P=\mathrm{diag}(1,1,0)$, compute $P|\psi\rangle$ and normalize.
\end{enumerate}

\section*{Practice B (uncertainty)}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Compute $\Delta \sigma_x$ and $\Delta \sigma_z$ for $|\psi\rangle=\cos(\theta/2)|0\rangle+e^{i\phi}\sin(\theta/2)|1\rangle$.
\item Verify Robertson bound for $A=\sigma_x$, $B=\sigma_z$.
\end{enumerate}

\section*{Practice C (POVM)}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Given $E_\pm=\frac12(I\pm \eta\sigma_z)$ compute $p(\pm)$ for a given Bloch vector state.
\end{enumerate}

\end{document}
```

## **S1 ‚Äî Variance in 2√ó2**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}
\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}
\geometry{margin=1in}
\begin{document}

\section*{L07-S1 Variance ‚Äî Problem}
Let $A=\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&-1\end{pmatrix}$ and $|\psi\rangle=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}\begin{pmatrix}1\\1\end{pmatrix}$.
Compute $\langle A\rangle$ and $(\Delta A)^2$.

\newpage
\section*{Suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Use $\langle A\rangle=\psi^\dagger A\psi$.
\item Use $(\Delta A)^2=\langle A^2\rangle-\langle A\rangle^2$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Advanced suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Note $A^2=I$ for this matrix.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Detailed solution}
$\psi=(1/\sqrt2,1/\sqrt2)^T$.
\[
\langle A\rangle=\psi^\dagger A\psi=(1/\sqrt2,1/\sqrt2)\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&-1\end{pmatrix}\begin{pmatrix}1/\sqrt2\\1/\sqrt2\end{pmatrix}=0.
\]
Since $A^2=I$, $\langle A^2\rangle=\psi^\dagger I\psi=1$.
Thus $(\Delta A)^2=1-0^2=1$.
\end{document}
```

## **S2 ‚Äî Commutator**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}
\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}
\geometry{margin=1in}
\begin{document}

\section*{L07-S2 Commutator ‚Äî Problem}
Let $A=\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&-1\end{pmatrix}$ and $B=\begin{pmatrix}0&1\\1&0\end{pmatrix}$.
Compute $[A,B]=AB-BA$.

\newpage
\section*{Suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Multiply matrices explicitly.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Advanced suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Recognize these as $\sigma_z$ and $\sigma_x$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Detailed solution}
\[
AB=\begin{pmatrix}0&1\\-1&0\end{pmatrix},\quad
BA=\begin{pmatrix}0&-1\\1&0\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Thus
\[
[A,B]=AB-BA=\begin{pmatrix}0&2\\-2&0\end{pmatrix}=2\begin{pmatrix}0&1\\-1&0\end{pmatrix}.
\]
\end{document}
```

## **S3 ‚Äî Compatibility example**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}
\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}
\geometry{margin=1in}
\begin{document}

\section*{L07-S3 Compatibility ‚Äî Problem}
Let $A=\mathrm{diag}(1,2)$ and $B=\mathrm{diag}(3,4)$. Show $[A,B]=0$ and explain why they are compatible (finite-dim case).

\newpage
\section*{Suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Diagonal matrices commute.
\item Recall commuting Hermitian matrices share an eigenbasis.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Advanced suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Explain that both are diagonal in the same basis, so can be measured together in that basis.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Detailed solution}
$AB=\mathrm{diag}(3,8)=BA$, hence $[A,B]=0$.
In finite dimension, commuting Hermitian operators are simultaneously diagonalizable, so there exists a basis of joint eigenvectors; measuring in that basis yields both values without ambiguity (compatibility in the ideal projective sense).
\end{document}
```

## **S4 ‚Äî Qubit variances**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}
\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}
\geometry{margin=1in}
\begin{document}

\section*{L07-S4 Qubit variances ‚Äî Problem}
Let $|\psi\rangle=\cos(\theta/2)|0\rangle+\sin(\theta/2)|1\rangle$ (real amplitudes).
Compute $\langle\sigma_z\rangle$ and $\Delta\sigma_z$.

\newpage
\section*{Suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Use $\langle\sigma_z\rangle=|\alpha|^2-|\beta|^2$.
\item Use $\sigma_z^2=I$ so $\Delta^2=1-\langle\sigma_z\rangle^2$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Advanced suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Express $\langle\sigma_z\rangle=\cos\theta$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Detailed solution}
Here $\alpha=\cos(\theta/2)$, $\beta=\sin(\theta/2)$.
\[
\langle\sigma_z\rangle=\cos^2(\theta/2)-\sin^2(\theta/2)=\cos\theta.
\]
Since $\sigma_z^2=I$, $\langle\sigma_z^2\rangle=1$, hence
\[
(\Delta\sigma_z)^2=1-\cos^2\theta=\sin^2\theta,\quad \Delta\sigma_z=|\sin\theta|.
\]
\end{document}
```

## **S5 ‚Äî Robertson bound for $$\sigma_x,\sigma_z$$**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}
\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}
\geometry{margin=1in}
\begin{document}

\section*{L07-S5 Robertson bound ‚Äî Problem}
For a normalized state $|\psi\rangle$ in $\mathbb C^2$, let $A=\sigma_x$, $B=\sigma_z$.
Show the Robertson bound reads $\Delta\sigma_x\,\Delta\sigma_z \ge |\langle\sigma_y\rangle|$.

\newpage
\section*{Suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Use $[\sigma_x,\sigma_z]=2i\sigma_y$.
\item Insert into $\Delta A\Delta B \ge \frac12|\langle[A,B]\rangle|$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Advanced suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Check factors: $\frac12|2i\langle\sigma_y\rangle|=|\langle\sigma_y\rangle|$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Detailed solution}
Since $[\sigma_x,\sigma_z]=2i\sigma_y$, Robertson gives
\[
\Delta\sigma_x\,\Delta\sigma_z \ge \frac12 | \langle 2i\sigma_y\rangle|
= |\langle\sigma_y\rangle|.
\]
\end{document}
```

## **S6 ‚Äî PVM probability + L√ºders update**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}
\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb,physics}
\geometry{margin=1in}
\begin{document}

\section*{L07-S6 L\"uders update (nondegenerate) ‚Äî Problem}
Let $P_0=|0\rangle\langle0|$ and $|\psi\rangle=\alpha|0\rangle+\beta|1\rangle$.
Compute $p(0)$ and the post-measurement state given outcome 0.

\newpage
\section*{Suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item $p(0)=\langle\psi|P_0|\psi\rangle$.
\item Updated state: $P_0|\psi\rangle/\sqrt{p(0)}$ if $p(0)>0$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Advanced suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Note $P_0|\psi\rangle=\alpha|0\rangle$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Detailed solution}
\[
p(0)=\langle\psi|0\rangle\langle0|\psi\rangle=|\alpha|^2.
\]
If $|\alpha|^2>0$, then
\[
|\psi'\rangle=\frac{\alpha|0\rangle}{|\alpha|}=e^{i\arg\alpha}|0\rangle \sim |0\rangle.
\]
Up to global phase, the state becomes $|0\rangle$.
\end{document}
```

## **S7 ‚Äî Degenerate L√ºders update in 3D**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}
\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}
\geometry{margin=1in}
\begin{document}

\section*{L07-S7 Degenerate L\"uders update ‚Äî Problem}
In $\mathbb C^3$, let $P=\mathrm{diag}(1,1,0)$ and $|\psi\rangle=(a,b,c)^T$.
Compute $p=\langle\psi|P|\psi\rangle$ and the updated state if outcome associated to $P$ occurs.

\newpage
\section*{Suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Compute $P|\psi\rangle=(a,b,0)^T$.
\item Normalize by $\sqrt{p}$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Advanced suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Interpret: outcome says ‚Äústate lies in the span of first two basis vectors‚Äù.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Detailed solution}
\[
p=\langle\psi|P|\psi\rangle=|a|^2+|b|^2.
\]
If $p>0$,
\[
|\psi'\rangle=\frac{(a,b,0)^T}{\sqrt{|a|^2+|b|^2}}.
\]
\end{document}
```

## **S8 ‚Äî POVM probabilities**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}
\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}
\geometry{margin=1in}
\begin{document}

\section*{L07-S8 POVM probabilities ‚Äî Problem}
Let $E_1=\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&1/2\end{pmatrix}$ and $E_2=I-E_1$.
For $|\psi\rangle=(\alpha,\beta)^T$ normalized, compute $p(1)=\langle\psi|E_1|\psi\rangle$ and $p(2)$.

\newpage
\section*{Suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Use $\langle\psi|E|\psi\rangle=(\alpha^*,\beta^*)E(\alpha,\beta)^T$.
\item Compute $E_2$ first.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Advanced suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Check $p(1)+p(2)=1$ automatically since $E_1+E_2=I$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Detailed solution}
\[
p(1)=|\alpha|^2+\frac12|\beta|^2.
\]
Also $E_2=\mathrm{diag}(0,1/2)$ so
\[
p(2)=\langle\psi|E_2|\psi\rangle=\frac12|\beta|^2.
\]
Sum: $p(1)+p(2)=|\alpha|^2+|\beta|^2=1$.
\end{document}
```

## **S9 ‚Äî Kraus to POVM and probabilities**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}
\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb}
\geometry{margin=1in}
\begin{document}

\section*{L07-S9 Kraus operators ‚Äî Problem}
Let $M_0=\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&\sqrt{1-\gamma}\end{pmatrix}$ and
$M_1=\begin{pmatrix}0&\sqrt{\gamma}\\0&0\end{pmatrix}$ with $0\le\gamma\le1$.
(i) Compute $E_i=M_i^\dagger M_i$. (ii) Show $E_0+E_1=I$. (iii) Compute $p(i)=\langle\psi|E_i|\psi\rangle$ for $|\psi\rangle=(\alpha,\beta)^T$.

\newpage
\section*{Suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Multiply $M_i^\dagger M_i$.
\item Use $\alpha,\beta$ normalization.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Advanced suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Recognize this as amplitude-damping Kraus form (physical interpretation optional).
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Detailed solution}
(i)
\[
E_0=M_0^\dagger M_0=\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&1-\gamma\end{pmatrix},\quad
E_1=M_1^\dagger M_1=\begin{pmatrix}0&0\\0&\gamma\end{pmatrix}.
\]
(ii) $E_0+E_1=I$.
(iii)
\[
p(0)=|\alpha|^2+(1-\gamma)|\beta|^2,\qquad p(1)=\gamma|\beta|^2.
\]
\end{document}
```

## **S10 ‚Äî PVM is a POVM**

```latex
\documentclass[11pt]{article}
\usepackage{geometry,amsmath,amssymb,physics}
\geometry{margin=1in}
\begin{document}

\section*{L07-S10 PVM as POVM ‚Äî Problem}
Let $\{P_a\}$ be projectors for a projective measurement. Show $\{E_a=P_a\}$ defines a POVM and $p(a)=\langle\psi|E_a|\psi\rangle$ matches the Born rule.

\newpage
\section*{Suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Check positivity: $P_a\ge0$.
\item Check completeness: $\sum_a P_a=I$.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Advanced suggestions}
\begin{itemize}
\item Explain what extra structure PVM has: orthogonality and idempotence.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section*{Detailed solution}
Projectors are positive and Hermitian, hence $E_a=P_a\ge0$, and $\sum_aE_a=I$.
Probabilities are $p(a)=\langle\psi|P_a|\psi\rangle$, which is precisely the projective Born rule.
\end{document}
```
